Total　　　2,500,934.89　　　261,655.94　　　2,239,278.95

Looking at the table above, it can be seen that the problem of telephone arrears is as serious as the problem of government telegram arrears. The reasons for telephone arrears, in addition to a few unscrupulous supervisors engaging in corruption and malpractice (this trend has been curbed since the Ministry of Communications strengthened rectification), also include the following points: A. Due to changes in the current situation, the indebted organizations and groups no longer exist; B. Various organizations and groups have not paid monthly rental fees due to changes in supervisors; C. Due to military influence, users have moved in a hurry and cannot be collected from; D. Businesses have closed down, resulting in no collection prospects; E. Although government agencies or businesses exist, they arbitrarily delay payment on the grounds of financial difficulties or business downturn. It is found that items A, C, and D are caused by sudden changes and user mobility, making it impossible to collect. However, these are accidental events of a temporary nature, not a permanent situation, and involve a small number of users, not a widespread phenomenon. Telephone bureau supervisors should pay close attention in advance to prevent them and take appropriate measures afterward to remedy them, and should not shirk responsibility due to changes in the situation. Items B and E do not have sufficient reasons! There have always been changes in supervisors of old agencies, and joint responsibility is clearly stipulated in the law. As for financial difficulties or business downturn, even if they are true, they are internal matters of the agency or business and have nothing to do with telephone fees. Before the agency is cancelled or the business closes down, the telephone bureau should strictly urge collection to value public funds, and users must not use one-sided reasons or other pretexts to evade and rely on them, disregarding the state-owned enterprise. Furthermore, the materials for telephone equipment are mostly purchased from overseas and are of great value. The price of a telephone set installed by a user is about 60 to 70 yuan for an automatic type and about 30 to 40 yuan for a common battery type. Therefore, a deposit and installation fee should be paid according to regulations at the time of installation. Many agencies pay this deposit as required, but there are also many who delay payment. Even due to the current situation, the personnel of the agency are scattered, and the telephone set also disappears. When another agency arises to replace it and needs telephone equipment urgently, the telephone bureau has no telephone sets in storage and no deposit to offset, so it is bound to submit a request to the Ministry of Communications to purchase new sets. The exchange of official documents delays the time, and users who need telephones see that they have not been installed for a long time, feel greatly inconvenienced, and even scold the telephone bureau for its ineffective handling. They do not deeply understand the telephone bureau's predicament due to accumulated arrears and the inability to do anything.

Since telephone equipment is more expensive than telegrams, and paying a deposit is more reliable than telegram fees, the monthly rental fee is usually only a few yuan to more than ten yuan, which is not as large as the telegram fee, which can be more than ten yuan or hundreds of yuan for one telegram. Moreover, local calls are only a few miles or tens of miles away, and the call time never includes the phrases "urgent" or "immediate arrival." This is the difference in the nature of telephone and telegraph services, and the difference in the ease of handling. Therefore, users must understand the difficulties of the telephone business and pay the monthly rental fee of only ten or so yuan or a few yuan on time. Otherwise, it is better to have the telephone removed to avoid dragging down the business. On the telephone bureau's side, it should strictly urge collection in accordance with the regulations of the ministry. On the other hand, it must approach users in various ways, verbally or in writing, to fully disclose the bureau's difficulties and explain the relationship between state-owned enterprises and the country and its people, to gain their understanding and then achieve the effect of concerted efforts.

It is heard that the Ministry of Communications has stipulated two measures for telephone arrears and ordered the bureaus to comply: (1) For old arrears that have collection prospects, collection should be stepped up. For those that have no collection prospects, a list of the user's name, amount of arrears, and whether there is a deposit should be submitted to the ministry for approval. (2) In the future, fees should be strictly collected according to regulations, and those who have not paid the deposit should immediately pay it, and there should be no more delays. After this reorganization, telephone arrears should come to an end, and the telephone bureau's revenue may improve?

Congratulations on the Success of Direct Communication Between China and Italy 283

— Zhongming

I have learned that there have long been discussions about direct communication between China and Italy. However, because the Rome Radio Station in the Italian capital and the Shanghai International Radio Station initially felt that the radio waves emitted by the Italian station were too weak and the wavelength was insufficient after testing communication, and the radio signals received by our side were not very clear, the Roman telecommunications authorities worked hard to improve, increase power, expand equipment, and conduct further tests. The results were excellent, the audio signals were exceptionally clear, and the speed was extremely fast. Therefore, formal communication began on the 21st of last month [October 21, 1934], and the business has been very prosperous. Therefore, I write what I feel to celebrate the success.

The introduction of Western culture to our country began with the arrival of the Italian Matteo Ricci in China during the Wanli period of the Ming Dynasty for missionary work. Subsequently, Italians Ferdinand Verbiest and Johann Adam Schall von Bell continued to come east during the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty, introducing sciences such as astronomy and mathematics, and at the same time introducing Eastern culture to the West. Therefore, the two great ancient countries of China and Italy hold the authority to communicate between East and West. Since the mutual elevation of ambassadors last year, the diplomatic relations have become even more cordial. Given the close relationship between the two countries, it is inevitable to feel that the lack of direct communication facilities is a flaw. Now that there is a direct telecommunications circuit between the two countries, it is expected that the diplomatic relations between the two countries will become even closer as a result. This is one reason. In the past, telecommunications between China and Italy, whether wireless or submarine cable, had to be relayed, which was too uneconomical in terms of time. From now on, telegrams between Shanghai and Rome can be sent directly, and telegrams from other places belonging to the two countries can be relayed by the two places, which is also faster than the previous relay. This is of great benefit to the business of the two countries. This is the second reason. It is estimated that the annual telegram fees spent between China and Italy amount to hundreds of thousands. In the past, due to the lack of direct circuits, these telegram fees inevitably leaked out and were at the mercy of others. With the existence of direct circuits, telegrams between the two countries can be handled by themselves, rather than relying on others. Since the leak has been plugged, the country will become richer. In view of the development of national and national thought among the people of the two countries in recent years, there is no reason to harm one's own interests for the benefit of others and damage one's own rights. This is very relevant to the future of telecommunications in both countries. This is the third reason. With these three reasons, it cannot be said that the telegraph services between China and Italy will not develop! This is my wish!

How to Use Telegrams? (Continued) 284

— Zhonghua

Regarding the "follow-up telegram" mentioned above, the sender often wants to know when it can be delivered properly. In that case, the telegraph bureau also has a convenient way. That is: the sender can ask the telegraph bureau to notify him immediately by telegram or mail after the delivery is completed. If a telegram is used, the sender only needs to add a "PC" to the recipient's name and address in the original telegram as a fee-paying mark, and only needs to prepay the ordinary telegram fee for six words. If a letter is used, the sender only needs to prepay the postage for a registered letter and add a "PCP" as a fee-paying mark. Sometimes, the sender is very anxious because he does not receive a reply from the recipient, so he can also use this delivery notification to prove that the recipient has indeed received it, which is very beneficial.

Regarding the content of the telegram, the telegraph bureau has always kept it absolutely confidential. Therefore, when the telegraph bureau sends a telegram to the recipient's name and address, the recipient must sign and stamp it to avoid being read by servants or other related people, which would lead to the disclosure of the telegram. In order to respect the interests of the recipient, the telegraph bureau has also formulated a "personal delivery telegram" method to remedy the above-mentioned shortcomings. The procedure for sending this "personal delivery telegram" is very simple. Just add a "MP" as a fee-paying mark. When the telegraph bureau at the receiving end sees a telegram with the "MP" mark, it will write "personal delivery" on the envelope and tell the messenger to deliver it to the recipient in person. In this way, the confidentiality of the telegram will be further guaranteed.

Some people think that "personal delivery telegrams" are still not very appropriate, because the recipient cannot stay in the office or residence all day long, so the "personal delivery telegram" can easily be delayed for a long time before it is received. Moreover, unless there has been contact beforehand, the telegraph bureau messenger cannot accurately prove the authenticity of the recipient. These practical difficulties are indeed unavoidable. Therefore, the telegraph bureau has also formulated another "hold for delivery" method, that is, the recipient goes to the telegraph bureau to pick it up himself, without going through the messenger's delivery procedure. In that case, the sender and receiver can absolutely maintain confidentiality and no longer have any worries. This "hold for delivery telegram" also has a convenience. For example, if the sender knows that the recipient has not yet arrived or has already left, he can allow the telegram to be temporarily held at the receiving bureau, waiting for the person or their representative to come to the bureau to pick it up in person, to avoid non-delivery. If the place where the telegram is to be received only has a post office and no telegraph bureau, then it can be handed over to the local post office for holding. The telegram held for delivery by the post office uses "GP" as a fee-paying mark. The telegram held for delivery by the telegraph bureau uses "TR" as a fee-paying mark. If it needs to be sent by registered mail by the post office, a separate registered postage fee must be added, and at the same time, "GPR" is used as a fee-paying mark.

The confidentiality of communication is certainly very important, but in some cases, it is not necessary to keep it confidential, or because of the need to keep it confidential, various inconveniences may arise. For example: A and B work in the same agency. A, as usual, returns home by car on Saturday night. Because of a temporary accident, he sends a telegram to B, asking him to ask for leave for a few days. It just so happens that B also asks for leave that day, so the telegram is placed on B's desk and no one cares about it. The colleagues in the agency, because they respect the confidentiality of communication between the two, of course do not want to open it. Therefore, A's leave procedures are not handled by anyone on his behalf, and he is eventually reprimanded by his superiors. Under these circumstances, the telegraph bureau also has a "sealed telegram" method to make up for the above-mentioned shortcomings. The so-called "sealed" means that the telegram envelope is not sealed and can be opened by anyone, so that anyone who sees it can immediately follow the meaning of the telegram and handle it, without having to wait for the recipient to handle it in person. This kind of sealed telegram uses "Ouvert" as a fee-paying mark.

Finally, the reporter wants to introduce a "cheap and good" special telegram. This kind of telegram is not directly sent by the sender, but it directly reduces the burden on the sender, and all readers can enjoy this special right. This is the "postal money order telegram"! In order to reduce the telegraph fees for people who use telegrams to remit money, the Ministry of Communications specially formulated a cheap money order telegram. No matter how much money you remit, as long as you go to the postal money order bureau to remit money, you only need to pay the appropriate exchange fee and a telegraph fee of six dimes. Among domestic telegrams, except for diplomatic telegrams, there is no telegram cheaper than six dimes. This preferential method is not enjoyed by people who go to banks to remit money. Readers, you might as well try it. (Ann)

Brief Biographies of World Telegraph Inventors 285

— Jian

1. Michael Faraday

Faraday was born in 1791 AD. He was an English scientist who made many inventions in chemistry, electricity, and magnetism, and was known for his time. In 1821, he first advocated that the rotation of a magnetic needle around an electric current was based on the theory of electromagnetism invented by Oersted in 1820. In 1831, he invented electromagnetic induction, and then created the basic principle of generator structure; in 1838, he invented the dielectric constant; in 1847, he invented the magnetic pole of light; the following year, he invented diamagnetism. He was a famous experimenter, and his contribution to modern electricity was particularly great.

2. Joseph Henry

Henry was born in 1797 AD and was an American physicist famous for his research on electromagnetism. After Sturgeon of England invented the electromagnet, Henry studied it in depth and made it a tool for extremely large electricity. In 1831, Henry used a thin copper wire about one mile long and an electromagnet to make the current attract the armature and strike a bell, thus forming the principle of modern telegraph application. In 1832, Henry was hired as a professor by Polingston University. In the school's laboratory, he used the principle of telegraph relay to configure the position of storage batteries and electromagnets, so that long-distance telegrams could be transmitted. He was the first to measure magnetic self-induction. In 1842, he specialized in oscillating discharge and studied other electrical phenomena. In 1846, he was elected as the secretary of the Washington Smithsonian Society. When he was working in the US Lighthouse Department, he also made important experiments such as maritime signals. Henry also conducted in-depth research on meteorology, geomagnetism, and acoustics. Henry has won international honors and is known as one of the most famous scientists in the United States.

3. William Thomson, Lord Kelvin

Kelvin was born in Belfast, England in 1824 AD. He entered Glasgow University at the age of ten. He graduated from Cambridge University in 1845. At the age of only twenty-two, he was hired as a professor of natural philosophy at Glasgow University and maintained his chair for fifty years with his outstanding talent. Around the age of forty, he was revered as a master of mathematics and science in England. His reputation was further enhanced by his important inventions in electrical telegraphs, compasses, and nautical instruments. He was awarded a knighthood in 1866 and a baronetcy in 1892. He died in 1907.

4. James Clerk Maxwell

Maxwell was born in Edinburgh, Scotland in 1831. He studied at Edinburgh and Cambridge Universities. From 1856 to 1869, he served as a professor of natural philosophy at Aberdeen University. From 1860 to 1865, he served as a professor of physics and astronomy at Kings College in London. In 1871, Maxwell was the first professor of experimental physics at the newly established Cambridge University. In his later years, Maxwell wielded the greatest authority in physics. His fame became more prominent after his death. Maxwell made many contributions to wireless telegraphy, especially electricity, which was his main research science throughout his life. In 1867, his first important paper, On Electromagnetic Theory, was praised by the Royal Society. In 1873, his immortal work, Electricity and Magnetism, was published. In the book, he explained the Electromagnetic Theory of Light and his Theory on Electric Waves, which was later verified by Hertz's experiments and created modern wireless telegraphy and telephones.

A Review of the Private Settlement of the Case of the Private Radio Station Set Up by Yongzengho Bank in Tianjin 286

— Diyou

The trial of the criminal part of the case of the private radio station set up by Yongzengho and Yongli Banks in Tianjin has been repeatedly recorded in this publication. As for the private compensation part, except for a part of Yongli Bank that has not yet been resolved, it is heard that Yongzengho has realized its mistake, sought mediation, and has reached a settlement. The situation is briefly described as follows:

After the criminal part of the case was sentenced by the Tianjin Court, the Tianjin Telegraph Bureau immediately began the private compensation procedures, requesting the court to provisionally seize the existing business income and all movable property of Yongzengho and Yongli Banks in accordance with Articles 488 and 489 of the Civil Procedure Law; and separately drafted a complaint to formally file a private lawsuit. While the above-mentioned provisional seizure was being ruled by the court, Yongzengho Bank immediately requested the Tianjin Bankers' Association to send a letter to the Telegraph Bureau, elaborating on the bank's remorse and willingness to compensate for the losses; at the same time, it entrusted Lawyer Kuai Jinde to send a letter to Lawyer Zhou Ze, the attorney of the Tianjin Bureau, to forward it to the Tianjin Bureau, briefly saying: "Yongzengho Bank has now designated the two million yuan of fixed deposits in Tianjin Bank of Communications under Liu Chaoqing's account on October 11 as security deposit in order to request the revocation of the provisional seizure. No withdrawals will be made before the compensation lawsuit is determined or the settlement is reached. If approved, please declare by your bureau to the court that the provisional seizure of that part will be temporarily suspended, and only the provisional seizure of Yongli Bank will be executed on a fixed-term basis to comply with the procedures. How should this be handled, please review and handle," etc. The Tianjin Bureau, according to the letter, considered that the two million yuan of fixed deposits in Tianjin Bank of Communications designated by the bank as a security deposit were not much different from the amount of 21,000 yuan requested by the bank for compensation. This method is not inconsistent with the law, and the bank also entrusted the Bankers' Association to come forward to request a settlement. The situation was sincere. In order to settle the matter and preserve the bank's business reputation, the bureau readily accepted the request and submitted a report to the Ministry of Communications for approval to pay the security deposit and revoke the provisional seizure of the bank's assets. At the same time, settlement procedures were carried out. As a result, the bank agreed to pay 17,000 yuan as compensation for the Tianjin Bureau's business losses, and the lawsuit was withdrawn, and the settlement was reached.

The Tianjin Bureau's telecommunications are extremely complete, and the transmission and reception of telegrams are fast and accurate, and has always been praised by Chinese and foreign people. However, the business house sent telegrams without using this legitimate and perfect institution, knowing that it was greedy for petty profits and did not hesitate to violate the law by setting up a private radio station. After the case was solved, the members of the number were either absconded for fear of crime, or were imprisoned. The body and spirit have suffered pain, and the business reputation has also been affected, and the private telegrams sent at ordinary times must still be paid for compensation. The magnitude of the loss was not what the bank initially expected. After this punishment, they deeply regretted their previous mistakes. Could those who set up private radio stations also know what to avoid?

Furthermore, it is heard that since the Ministry of Communications solved this case, the crackdown on private radio stations has become more serious. It has reiterated a clear order to telegraph institutions in various places to conduct strict investigations at any time, and the major telegraph bureaus in the major ports have published advertisements and offered rewards to encourage secret reports (the names of informants are kept absolutely confidential). It is found that private radio stations, on a small scale, disrupt finance and damage the market, and on a large scale, spread rumors and affect public security, or even provide resources for the enemy, endangering the country. The harm is too great to describe. It is hoped that people in society will share this understanding and help together. For everything heard and seen that involves the illegal establishment of radio stations, please report it at any time in a confidential letter to the local Ministry of Communications Telegraph Bureau or Radio Station, or directly report it to the Telegraph Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing, so as to conduct investigations and confiscate them and strictly enforce national laws. It is thought that this is also what those who are enthusiastically patriotic are happy to do.

Discussing Two Types of Telegrams Serving Society 287

— Qinghua

Telegrams are divided into several types, such as government affairs, urgent, ordinary, news, social, and official business. Except for official business telegrams, which are sent internally by the telegraph office for official purposes and are not charged, all other types of telegrams are charged uniformly, but the prices vary. In addition, there are two other types of telegrams that are transmitted free of charge by the telegraph office: meteorological telegrams and disaster relief telegrams. The former is of great importance to navigation safety, and the latter is related to disaster relief in disaster areas. The telegraph office is specially authorized to transmit them free of charge, with the intention of serving society!

However, due to the free nature of the above two types of telegrams, redundancy is inevitable, which not only consumes more materials for the telegraph office, but also clogs the circuits, affecting the transmission speed of other types of telegrams. Therefore, from the perspective of the telegraph office, if redundancy is found, strict restrictions are the only option.

First, let's talk about meteorological telegrams.

Meteorological telegrams are telegrams in which meteorological agencies report meteorological observations or meteorological forecasts. International telegrams are charged at half the price of ordinary telegrams in accordance with Article 73 of the International Telegraph Regulations. For domestic telegrams, the Ministry of Communications, in view of the small number of meteorological agencies in China and their mostly inadequate finances, has specially authorized free transmission. However, in recent years, the number of meteorological agencies has gradually increased. In addition to the existing observatories in Shanghai and Qingdao, there are now the Central Meteorological Research Institute, the Aviation Committee, meteorological stations run by the Shandong and Jiangsu Construction Bureaus, and the Shanxi Agricultural College. In order to carry out meteorological forecasting, the above-mentioned meteorological agencies need to collect reports of meteorological observations from various places. Therefore, the number of agencies sending meteorological telegrams is extremely large, such as customs houses, aviation stations, and county governments, totaling more than 200. Each agency sends meteorological telegrams twice a day, totaling more than 400 times. Some agencies even send telegrams to two meteorological agencies at the same time, making the number of telegrams even more numerous. As a result, the telegraph office, due to the free nature of meteorological telegrams, inevitably transmits fee-based telegrams first, and then meteorological telegrams, so a small number of meteorological telegrams are inevitably delayed, and meteorological agencies express dissatisfaction as a result. The Ministry of Communications has recently taken this into account, believing that meteorological telegrams are related to navigation safety. Since free transmission is allowed, they should be transmitted quickly so that they can be effective in a timely manner. Otherwise, when they reach the meteorological agencies, they are already outdated, useless to the meteorological agencies, and waste labor and materials for the telegraph office, which is very uneconomical. However, there should be a systematic organization of national meteorological agencies to avoid each acting on its own. For example, the meteorological stations run by the Jiangsu and Shandong Construction Bureaus are not connected with the Central Meteorological Research Institute, so most of the meteorological telegrams sent from various places are redundant, which is inevitable for redundancy. It is now heard that the Ministry of Communications is discussing with the Central Meteorological Research Institute and the Aviation Committee on the organization of a meteorological communication network, so that meteorological telegrams can achieve the greatest effect at the smallest cost, so that both parties feel convenient. Before this communication network is formed, the Ministry of Communications has first ordered various telegraph offices to quickly transmit meteorological telegrams, and has stipulated abbreviations for various receiving meteorological agencies, such as OBSER for ordinary meteorological agencies and OBSAV for aviation meteorological agencies, so that the number of telegram words is reduced and transmission can be faster. At the same time, it also ordered the Nanjing Telegraph Office to contact the Central Meteorological Research Institute, which receives the most telegrams, to install a dedicated telephone line, so that when the telegraph office receives meteorological telegrams from various places, it can use the telephone to transmit them, which is faster than sending them by messengers. This is the greatest effort of the telegraph office to serve, and it is hoped that the Central Research Institute will come forward to seek a systematic organization of meteorological agencies in China, and strive to reduce unnecessary meteorological telegrams (referring to avoiding duplication, etc.), which will undoubtedly be of great benefit to meteorological observations!

Next, let's talk about disaster relief telegrams.

Disaster relief telegrams were originally set up for temporary emergency relief. Anyone sending disaster relief telegrams must first apply to the Ministry of Communications for a free disaster relief telegram permit, with a maximum period of six months. Each telegram must not exceed 100 words. The restrictions were originally very strict, but in recent years, natural and man-made disasters have come one after another in China, so that charitable organizations and disaster relief agencies have never ended their disaster relief efforts, and the disaster relief telegram permits have been extended again and again. Recently, more disaster relief agencies have emerged, so that disaster relief telegrams are becoming increasingly numerous. According to regulations, disaster relief telegrams should be limited to emergency relief. If they are ordinary and not urgent relief matters, they can be contacted by proxy telegrams. But in fact, now various disaster relief agencies send telegrams at every turn, with lengthy sentences. The telegraph office not only consumes materials, but also greatly affects other fee-based telegrams, which violates the original intention of free preferential treatment! It has been found that there is no provision for disaster relief telegrams in the domestic telegram regulations of various countries. It was initially thought that disasters and famines were rare in European, American, and Japanese countries, so there were no provisions for disaster relief telegrams. However, in fact, the great earthquake in Tokyo, Japan in 1923 caused great harm. At that time, the telegrams sent by Japanese charitable organizations for emergency relief were all paid for at the price of ordinary telegrams, and there was no request for free treatment. Floods and droughts occur every year in European and American countries, and there is no method of sending telegrams free of charge. Furthermore, domestic railway bureaus charge full fares for disaster relief personnel to ride trains and charge half price for transporting disaster relief clothing and grain. The post office also charges fees for disaster relief correspondence in accordance with regulations. It can be seen that the free disaster relief telegram is actually a unique example at home and abroad. It is hoped that various disaster relief agencies will make good use of it and automatically reduce the number of telegrams and the number of words, so that the free preferential treatment will not be changed due to redundancy.

Semi-Monthly News 288

— Qinghua

The Guangdong Provincial Telegraph Bureau Stops Charging Line Repair Fees

The telegraph bureaus in Guangdong Province previously believed that the telegraph lines in Guangdong Province were severely damaged and urgently needed to be repaired in order to maintain communication. However, the telegraph funds were insufficient, and it was not easy to raise funds for line repairs. Therefore, it was specially stipulated that domestic telegrams would be charged an additional 30% of the line repair fee per word (i.e., ordinary telegrams would be charged 1.3 yuan per word) to be used for line repair fees. The Ministry of Communications believed that although the additional line repair fee was prepared for proper line repairs, it increased the burden on the public and was different from the telegram prices in other provinces, which was unfair. Therefore, it has ordered the telegraph bureaus in Guangdong Province to stop charging the additional fee from January 1 to ensure uniformity.

Supplement to the Shen Bao in This City

Talking Points

Six Days of Winter Vacation 289

— Long

During the six days of this newspaper's suspension for the winter vacation, there were certainly many changes in the world, at home, and even in this city that could serve as material for discussion. Here are a few of the more valuable events, briefly discussed.

First, the market in this city has been on a downward spiral in recent years, especially during the Lunar New Year, which is the most tense. Before the Lunar New Year, it was expected that the Lunar New Year last year would bring about an unprecedented economic downturn. However, last year's Lunar New Year, except for a few banks experiencing small-scale turmoil, was gradually calmed down due to sufficient reserves. It was still able to be celebrated peacefully amidst the sounds of drums and congratulations. In addition, after the holiday, many stores will inevitably fail to open their doors, but that is a matter for later, so let's not talk about it now.

Second, the issue of Japan's invasion of Chahar initially seemed very tense. Later, thanks to the efforts of diplomats, a large-scale conference was held, and the situation in eastern Chahar eased. As for the results of the discussion and the extent of the loss of our country's rights, we can ignore them for now. However, it is heard that the Japanese army can withdraw completely after the meeting. If so, the Chahar incident can be considered to have come to an end, and the incident will not expand further, which can be considered getting by.

Third, the issue of the European situation. On February 3 (i.e., Lunar New Year's Eve), the United Kingdom and Japan established the London Agreement. This matter is of utmost importance to the issue of European peace. Because among the European powers, the strongest are the United Kingdom, France, Italy, and Germany, and Germany is in a position of antagonism with the other three countries. Moreover, its ambitions are high and its actions are perverse, causing everyone to look askance. However, the United Kingdom, France, and Italy cannot fully agree on how to deal with Germany due to their different positions and conflicting interests. Now, thanks to the efforts of French Foreign Minister Laval, the Rome Agreement was established with Italy, and the London Agreement was established with the United Kingdom. Thus, the three countries jointly cooperate to contain the powerful enemy, so the chances of success can be grasped. Therefore, the Italian Foreign Minister said, "1935 can be said to be an important year for peace building." That is the meaning of this.

Vagrants 290

— Xu Ying

Like summer, the sky is so clear, sparkling with bright stars. But it's cold, the roadside trees have shed their leaves, the earth is exposed in its bareness. The Bohai Sea wind is also cold, flowing in along the Bai River, stinging the pores like knives. Vagrants, without proper leisure, lie on the short cement wall, blowing a tuneless tune, sinking their hearts into the dark depths, quietly counting the stars in the clear sky.

The cold driving force dispelled the vagrants' optimism. Groups of them, scattered here and there, or scattered sporadically, slowly gathered in the city center from the parks, from the streets, from the empty teahouses, from the ice-cellar-like hostels. The hustle and bustle of the city can shake the hearts of the hungry and cold, and the neon lights that twist like dragons can trigger a trace of warmth in human cells.

The cold wind caresses everything on the earth, treating the skyscrapers and the smallest grain of soil equally. The cold wind detracts from the color of the city center, the cold wind makes pedestrians hesitate, the cold wind makes people in heavy fur coats feel stiff even sitting in cars. The cold wind sweeps more than half of the street pedestrians to the night market.

At night, the vagrants have to enjoy a moment of warmth in the night market.

From the time the electric lights are turned on, the night market is populated. The peddlers also light their dim yellow oil lamps, giving their wares a faint shadow. It is unorganized, yet seems organized, with each stall on the street having a fixed location. After dinner time, the police carry large white cloth bags to collect stall donations, which start at a large copper coin.

The crowd gathers here, and here there is heat, there is strength, there is vitality. The small restaurants especially bang their frying pans loudly, and the flames from the stove make the faces of passersby turn red; the hoarse voices of the used clothing stalls are louder than each other, like several violins playing music without rosin; sellers and buyers are talking in raised voices, and when the buyer takes a few steps, the seller calls him back in an even louder voice, but the buyer refuses to turn around, and the two renegotiate the price at a distance of one hundred meters.

There are many people in the noisy crowd, but not many people come to buy things. The vagrant groups are deliberately warming themselves, and sometimes, perhaps if the opportunity is good, they can incidentally earn a little money. If it is goods, they are passed hand-to-hand to the pawnshop to exchange for money. Friends on the streets are righteous, everyone eats and drinks when they have money, and then they disperse in a rush.

In the night market, the stench is mixed with fragrance. In addition to groceries, there are also many late-night snacks. On the cold meat stalls, the halal stalls display whole pig heads with kind and benevolent eyes, while the Muslim stalls display large pieces of animal meat, which are black like a pile of buffalo dung; the congee vendors are surrounded by a thin mist, and people come and go in the hazy atmosphere. In addition, there are stalls selling sheep intestines, wontons, and sesame cakes, each with its own smell and posture.

Sometimes, it is precisely the brothers who are eating happily at these stalls. The black-clad police, together with the gray-clad informants, walk into the misty atmosphere and pat a vagrant on the shoulder, saying;

"Brother, your case is over!"

This brother then naturally drinks the last cup of wine, and without saying a word, lets others tie the white rope tightly on his arm, knowingly glancing around with his expressive eyes to inform the other vagrant groups. Why? The rules of the streets.

If, unfortunately, a hand is in someone else's pocket, he will be grabbed by the arm, which is the most disgraceful thing. At this time, this person must escape desperately. If the wind is favorable and someone is covering him, the vagrant groups will obstruct traffic, and people will be squeezed everywhere. When cars, horses, and people are all noisy, the pickpocket's catcher can only sigh in vain.

The vagrant groups watch the moon in the night year after year. If you ask how many shooting stars there are this year, they will be the first to know. It's just that the place is different. This year it's on the Bohai Sea coast, but last year it was on the ancient city walls. Next year, maybe it will be at the mouth of the Yangtze River.

Whether it is on the Bohai Sea coast, whether it is on the ancient city walls, whether it is at the mouth of the Yangtze River, as long as there is a night market, this scene will always appear.

Mao's Envy 291

— Yi An

Yearning and Others 292

— Ye Jian

"A child born of wandering will never understand any yearning!"

Leaving my sick mother, leaving her, leaving my desolate hometown, leaving the bronze-colored moon every night, finally, I wandered out again.

Life seems to harbor a special hatred for me, but it also seems to harbor a special love. At such a young age, when others were being placed by their loving mothers in soft cradles, I was being illuminated by a more peculiar gaze. I am forever writhing in her arms. She makes me happy, and she makes me cry; she makes me brave, and she makes me frustrated. She smiles kindly at me, and she glares fiercely at me: I am a helpless, stubborn child.

Yes, I understand very well: a child who has rolled out of life's furnace, from the barren wilderness, is not easily compromised, nor is he very obedient.

I didn't even need to discover this myself. Even the mother who personally arranged my growth, and she who had been playing mud dolls with me since I was six years old, said in amazement:

"How strange: has he become so cruel? Nothing can arouse his yearning, nothing can earn his attachment."

It is true. All the childhood longings, infatuations, and hobbies have been completely shattered in the process of wandering. The family's intimate tone, her youthful

Page 24

young smile, the camellias on the hillside in front of the door, the multicolored roof peaks of the ancient temple, the sun hanging on the branches at dusk... even when they appear in my dreams, they only make people reveal a bitter face. So, year after year, I have lived through it, and I have a kind of perception like a bas-relief: hazy and flat. I have learned to use ignorance to cope with a smile, a stimulus, a sorrow, just as I use intuition to accept a mountain, a river, a pile of dead branches... my thoughts are flattened, numbed.

So, I understand: I am ultimately happy, I am happy.

One day, it was late autumn, I was walking in the wilderness, a pile of ashes from dead branches lay in front of me. I looked at it, and looked at it again, and several images occurred in a peculiar succession before my eyes: a scattering of seeds, a cluster of seedlings, a row of tender branches, a falling leaf, a section of dead trunk, a pile of ashes. From the tragedy of seeds and ashes, I seemed to receive an enlightenment: a wandering origin, a wandering end. I hoped that a north wind would blow, I hoped to see the ashes swirling in the air. So, I fantasized about a grain of ash, floating, aimlessly, unknowingly, settling on an unfamiliar land. People trample on it, people neglect it, people forget it, and day by day, it is so pressed into the distant strata. It is a tragedy of nature.

So, I began to learn cruelty, I learned indifference, I learned the principles of the tragedy of nature.

In this way, even I became a little confused: what is worth yearning for? A smile? The sun? This flowing stream and purple mountain peaks? Or the unreliable disguise of human passion, and nature, which is the performance of tragedy?

Really, you say, what can a child born of wandering yearn for?

Then: forget the feelings, forget the attachments, forget the thoughts, forget the yearnings. In the process of wandering, cruelty is ignorance; and ignorance is always happiness.

Trembling, throwing everything behind me, I finally wandered out again. I remember a sentence:

"Coming naked and going without attachments!"

Its greatness made me shudder.

Amateur Mailbox

Wanting to Find a Way Out Through Literature 293

Editor:

I am an eighteen-year-old child, currently living in a difficult environment. Although I want to strive for the future, I don't know if there will be a day of success in striving like this. So, I am telling you my current situation and my direction of advancement, hoping that you can give me a clear indication.

Since I was seven years old, my father sent me to a sailboat dedicated to sailing on the Yangtze River to do cooking work. After working hard for several years, at the age of thirteen, I started working as a boatman pulling poles and ropes. During this period, I was rolled by waves several times, and there was often a danger of losing my life.

At the age of fourteen, I moved from Ningbo to Shanghai. I stopped being a boatman, and my father provided tuition, so I became a student. But after the January 28th Incident, I was declared to have dropped out of school. Later, fortunately, through the introduction of my father's friend, I went to a school run by the Ministry of Communications that did not require tuition and studied for two years, and finally graduated. But it was also the time when the difficulties of life attacked me. I don't want to continue my studies anymore, because I really don't have the ability to study. But I have nothing to do. Sir, my family of six or seven people eats, and my father is just a peddler selling socks, and I don't work, how can this be maintained? So, the situation of life difficulties is really unimaginable. As for myself, I am idle every day, running around aimlessly, and what I am most interested in is going to the Shen Bao Circulation Library. Because there I can see many books without spending a penny. Also, because I can't afford the one or two yuan deposit, I have to run there every day. But sometimes, the good book that I can't finish reading today is borrowed by someone else tomorrow, and I can't continue reading it, how painful is that at that time! Of course, no matter what, reading a little good book is better than not reading at all.

Recently, I have been very fond of reading literature books. I desperately read those works by famous Chinese and foreign writers, and at the same time, it seems to arouse the hope in my heart, so I tried writing. And for economic reasons, I started submitting articles, hoping to get a little稿費to maintain my life. However, the results were all returned one after another, probably because the skills were too bad? So, I am now going to continue to work hard on writing, I want to抄出a way out from the literary aspect. But can I reach my goal!

Sir, I am now attaching my recent works, hoping that you can give me a stern criticism, and I hope you can give me some instructions on the writing method, hoping for it! Respectfully, respectfully

Write and rest, Long Chen 上

Editor's note: After reading your letter, knowing the truth about your painful life, I am very sad for you in my heart. At the same time, I see that you are struggling very hard to the environment, and there is no attitude of厭世or sorrow, which makes me feel that you are very admirable.

You are now studying literature, which is very good; but there is one thing you need to understand, that is, studying literature is not specifically to solve the problem of personal food, if you only work hard for personal food, then the article will not have great promise. Of course, a person always has to eat, but studying literature must never be specifically for personal food.

To study literature, it is not enough to study only in the scope of literature, you must also study a little social science at the same time. You must clearly recognize this society, and then you can see clearly your position in society; in this way, your article will have very good content. If you only study literature itself or its techniques, then your article at most has a little progress in technique, flowing to虛華, and the content must be unfulfilled.

I have already read your three manuscripts, and the writing skills have achieved considerable results, but the content is still insufficient. Therefore, you should still focus on studying and doing things in the future, learn more theories, experience more events, and the content will gradually be fulfilled. Regarding the failure of submitting articles, don't be discouraged, you should continue to learn and write, as long as you are willing to work hard, then you will always have the hope of success in the future.

The difficulties of life are now a very common phenomenon, and there are so many people who are more difficult than you, so you don't have to lose your spirit of progress because of the oppression of life, you should continue to fight the environment, and there is absolutely nothing that cannot be solved.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Examining the Hollywood Divorce History of 1935: A Review of the Fairbanks-Pickford Divorce 298

— Huang Yingdai

According to a Los Angeles dispatch, the court has granted a separation to screen couple Douglas Fairbanks and Mary Pickford. This event occupies an important page in the history of Hollywood film stars' divorces in 1935. When we recall that Douglas Fairbanks and Mary Pickford had been married since 1920, and have now lived together for fifteen years, most people thought that this couple would grow old together. Who knew that things would turn out unexpectedly? The protagonists of this divorce case did not break up in the middle of those fifteen years, but instead separated in their later years. It is truly said that silver screen couples are fickle and can divorce at any time!

If we recall, in those fifteen years, rumors of separation between Mary Pickford and Douglas Fairbanks had already emerged in the early years of their marriage. But after the parties denied it, these rumors died down. In Hollywood, this silver kingdom, the separation and reunion of silver screen couples are inherently unstable, and rumors about marriage and divorce are spread every day. Therefore, the public regarded the Fairbanks' divorce as just another common rumor. However, in the recent three years, the rumors have become even more intense, and at the beginning of 1935, this divorce case has turned from rumor into reality.

When they got married, Mary Pickford and Douglas Fairbanks were both in their golden age; one was the Queen of Cinema, and the other was the Emperor of Cinema. In the film industry, both were very popular; moreover, they were both among the wealthiest stars. At the time of their union, they shared the same interests in their careers and in their hearts; they were both first-class stars in Hollywood; their positions in the film industry were very stable. They were both reputable people, both loved making friends, and both were devoted to the film industry. Wasn't their union the ideal match? This is evidenced by the fact that after their marriage, the couple always shared a few sweet kisses before going to the film set, and Mary always bid farewell with tears in her eyes when Douglas went on long trips. After Douglas and Mary got married, they did not dance with other women for more than ten years, so one can imagine how deep their love was after marriage.

The past rumors were nothing but unfounded gossip, but in the recent three to five years, there have been repeated rumors of divorce between Douglas Fairbanks and Mary Pickford, and in these rumors, we can see that their feelings are no longer as harmonious as before. What were the reasons for Mary and Douglas's divorce? Although there are various rumors, the filming of "The Taming of the Shrew" was a major sticking point. Although Douglas Fairbanks and Mary Pickford had been married for fifteen years, they had only co-starred in one film, "The Taming of the Shrew," but as a result of filming this movie, the two sides had different opinions and insisted on their own views, causing a major conflict. After that, their opinions became even more incompatible, and as a result, the love between the couple broke down, leading to their separation.

This divorce case was of course initiated by Mary Pickford, and Douglas Fairbanks, who was approaching old age, wanted to maintain their marriage at all costs; therefore, after the rift between him and Mary Pickford, he ran to England. His purpose was nothing more than to ease the conflict and reduce Mary's anger, so that when he returned to the United States, they could reconcile and easily live in harmony again. Who knew that Douglas Fairbanks' trip to London could not quell Mary's anger. After returning to the United States, although people within the circle mediated, Mary still insisted on her divorce proposal. Finally, not long after the curtain rose on 1935, the Los Angeles court, in three minutes, ruled the divorce case valid. From then on, this so-called ideal silver screen couple went their separate ways, and everything in the past was just adding some memories to their lives.

Film Review

Review of "The Night Before the Wedding" 299

— You Jing

丨Paris Projection丨

At a time when foreign aggression is rampant and the people's morale is declining, "The Night Before the Wedding" allows us to hear the tragic, magnificent, and passionate war song: "Fight, fight, fight, all rush to the front line...

Avenge our hatred and snow, and bravely strive to be first" and "Kill, kill, kill, the great war has broken out, the country is in danger, quickly save China," which is worthy of our seeking and recommending its meaning.

Unfortunately, due to the outdated selection of themes and expression techniques, it not only blurs the meaningful impression it gives to the audience, but also makes the audience doubt the personality contradictions of the main character, the officer Yuan Xinghai, thus affecting the effect that the author attempts and strives to achieve.

The personality contradictions of Yuan Xinghai are clearly expressed in the two songs he sings himself: "Light Boat on the Lake" and "War Song." The former writes out the type of "chocolate candy officer" as the West calls it and the "hanging dandy soldier" as the Chinese vernacular says: chasing women, making triangle love, etc. The latter says that he is so "determined to sacrifice himself to do it," and actually completes his will of "men die on the battlefield" and "wrapped in horsehide." Without a proper and sufficient process in between, the two different personality prototypes are abrupt and contradictory before and after, and under the positive and negative, they are transformed into a "non-existent illusion."

Here, let's discuss the technical aspects of "The Night Before the Wedding." Because it is a "full sound white singing" film, then let's start with the dubbing and dialogue:

Speaking of dubbing, with the current material and technical limitations of Chinese sound films, some shortcomings in sound are originally not too demanding, but the impropriety of the dubbing is an undeniable fact. For example, in this "Night Before the Wedding," such as the scene where Li Minghui was chased home by Yuan Congmei to sleep, when Li raised her powder leg and smiled, accompanied by such an unharmonious and strong sound, I don't know what its function is? Here, the sound and picture not only cannot multiply each other, but also damage each other.

In terms of dialogue, in addition to a few places that are incomprehensible, such as saying "no personality" as "no qualifications, no humanity," it is improper, such as the dialogue between the two protagonists when reading love and love, the tone is too uninflected, resulting in a breath and grammar of anger and quarrel. As well as the unnecessary time and space for the dialogue, the dialogue repeats before and after the book and cannot play a role of multiplication and benefit.

The book weaving is also inevitable to lose to sluggishness, annoyance; slackness, such as when the officer tells the woman's father that he will sacrifice everything to love his daughter, the expressions of the uncle outside the door, the daughter upstairs, and the four people cannot make simultaneous, unified and different reflections, and when the officer and lover say goodbye to the woman's father on the night before the wedding, three faces cannot be woven into one picture, and so on.

The whole film deals with several scenes of war better.

Review of "New Woman" 丨丨 Jin Cheng 300

— Ling He

Previously, there was "Three Modern Women" that appeared on the Chinese film scene in a brand new posture, making Chinese films begin to have new changes. It had epoch-making significance, which is what people cannot ignore. The playwright of the film put forward three different women: one is a pleasure-seeking social flower, one is a petit-bourgeois woman who believes in love first, and the other is a female worker. Which of these three women is the most modern? The playwright clearly indicates that the female worker is the darling of the times, shouldering the historical task, while the disillusionment of the petit-bourgeois woman's love dreams and the pleasure-seeking of capitalist social flowers are all satirized and cursed. 丨丨 In this respect, it is a successful work.

Two years later, we have seen this new woman with a content that is quite similar to "Three Modern Women." The playwright also put forward three women of the same era but of different essence: one is Mrs. Wang, who quarrels with her comprador husband for a car to ride in and hooks up with actors, the same as the female worker Aying, and the other is a female writer who has a certain degree of self-awareness, but cannot withstand the torment of society, and commits suicide in contradictory life.

So, who is the new woman here? Although the playwright tries his best to describe the female writer's self-awareness, the contradiction between life and will ultimately leads her to commit suicide. In the end, although she has the confidence to work hard to live, hoping to endure hardship and become independent with her sister who lives with her, it is too late, she has been eliminated by the times. And Mrs. Wang's licentiousness is given a poisonous satire by the playwright. The suggestion of a new woman is naturally on the female worker Aying, and the theme song "New Woman Song" also directly explains this point: "The new woman is the production masses; ······ is the social labor, ······ is the vanguard of building a new society. New women, want to be with men······ Don't be slaves, the world is for the public! Regardless of men and women, the world is one! New women, bravely rush forward! "Yes, the new woman's life is simple, she doesn't dream of love. After Wei Ming died, they trampled on the news of her death in the newspaper and rushed forward.

Like "Three Modern Women," the playwright's analysis and understanding of the female group is correct, which is naturally very powerful for the lessons of intellectual women. Therefore, we only require the enrichment of the content of the work, and as for the similarity of the theme to other works, it cannot of course be regarded as a shortcoming of "New Woman." However, the theme seems to be more clichéd, so that the particularity of the work cannot be displayed, and there are still some shortcomings in the drama skills, and there are also many very dramatic places.

From the evaluation of the entire work, due to the relationship of the objective environment, and because Ruan Lingyu's grasp of the posture of intellectual women is not deep enough, and the dubbing has some shortcomings except for the final steam whistle that has a very good stimulus, it cannot make the work reach a completely successful level. But we can never deny that it is a fairly mature film. The screenwriter, director, photography, composer, dubbing setting, and even every actor are doing their work with the greatest efforts. We look forward to their greater success in the future.

The Exchange of Film and Drama 301

— Luo Fu

Since the news of the performance of the Stage Association in Jin Cheng was announced, this cannot but make people feel gratified. At the beginning of this 1935, it is exciting that people who have gone from the stage to the screen, and most of the people who are active in drama, can cooperate so closely and hold large-scale public performances.

Taking January 28 as the dividing line, Chinese films have undergone new changes, and part of the reason is that the stage people have entered the film field, making them active as a driving force. But on the other hand, drama itself has been silent because of this. On the one hand, economic environment and other relations have hindered the progress of drama, and on the other hand, the fact that people who specialize in drama have been attracted by films is also a major reason. It is precisely because of the above two reasons that the Chinese drama movement has not given the audience a full understanding, because there is no lovely success in technology.

Now, there are very good objective conditions. The Shanghai-style Peking opera is actively falling into decline, and the general movie theaters that often sell seats with song and dance can no longer be summoned. They all demand that spoken dramas be staged, which is of great help to improving the drama atmosphere, so the slogan that 1935 is the year of drama is shouted.

The first public performance of the Stage Association is naturally the first shot of 1935, and the broad audience is eagerly expecting this public performance to have a great success. Yes, we expect that such a public performance with so many talents should at least be a more standard activity in terms of technology. The exchange of film and drama, we wish them great success!

Film Novel

David Copperfield (1) 302

— Liu Cun

Produced by MGM, starring Lionel Barrymore, Louis Easton, etc.

David Copperfield first saw Mr. Murdstone in the chapel. Later, he gradually remembered how he met him, but it happened in a place of benevolence and righteousness, wasn't it the reversal of nature's impermanence. It was a warm summer Sunday. His widowed mother and the benevolent Peggotty, one of their maids, were happily gathered in a very small chapel. David was very happy, until he saw Mr. Murdstone looking at his mother. Although he was a very young child, he already felt that that person was not to be approached. The first time he saw him, he shivered and clung tightly to his mother's skirt, as if afraid that he would grab him.

He whispered to his mother: "Mom, that person, he's like a black panther in my animal book." His mother quickly forbade him: "Lower your voice! He is a friend of Mom's, don't say that." From then on, every time he saw Mr. Murdstone, he thought of that treacherous and terrifying black panther in the book, which made him feel uneasy. But he soon realized that his fear at that time was nothing, until Mr. Murdstone came to live in his and his dear mother's house, that was truly terrible. He made him tremble with fear.

He felt inexplicably why his mother hurriedly sent him into the car, driven by a Barkis, and asked him to go to Yarmouth and stay with Peggotty's relatives for a while. David didn't understand why his mother stayed at home and didn't go, but Peggotty told him that she was also going to stay at her friend's house for a few days. David accepted this explanation and tried his best to enjoy this trip, but he didn't know that this was the last time he had some happiness in many years.

He was very happy at Peggotty's house. In addition to Peggotty, who lived with him, there was Ham, Peggotty's nephew, Miss Gummidge, a close friend, who was always frowning, and Dan Peggotty, who was the brother of the old fisherman Peggotty. In addition, what David felt was lovely in his mind was little Em'ly, who often played with David on the beach. But what he found most interesting was the house they lived in. But that can't be considered a house. It was really just a broken ship that was placed high on the shore, with the bottom of the ship facing the sky, and a steel pipe standing upright on the top, which was the chimney of the house. There were also beautiful small doors and small windows, all opened on the side of the ship. David thought, how interesting it is to live in a boat on the ground!

When David came to Yarmouth, although Peggotty had told him not to ask too many questions, he soon found out that the rude and strong, but benevolent old fisherman, was an old bachelor. He supported so many people, Ham was his brother's son, Em'ly was his sister's daughter, and Miss Gummidge was the woman who accompanied him. The fathers or husbands of these people all died in the ruthless sea of anger and torrents, white waves and滔天.

But these past tragedies did not depress David and Em'ly's mood when they were wandering on the beach. Em'ly also told him that her heartfelt wish was that if she could become a noblewoman in the future, she would definitely buy Uncle Peggotty a blue coat with diamond buttons.

Finally, his trip was over, and he and Peggotty had to go back to see his mother. He was eager to return all the way, thinking of his loving mother. When his car arrived at the door, he jumped out of the car and ran straight into the house to see his mother. But as soon as he entered the door, he stopped abruptly. His mother was in the house, sitting in the old place by the fireplace as usual, but on that side was sitting the black panther, the person he saw in the chapel, Mr. Murdstone. He couldn't help but look at Peggotty's face in suspicion. Peggotty whispered, "That's your new dad." (To be continued)
